<div id="review_3296941478" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3296941478" />
    <a title="Mary ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37766180-mary"><img alt="Mary ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1555156334p2/37766180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3296941478?book_show_action=true">May 22, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary ♥" href="/user/show/37766180-mary">Mary ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3296941478" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13659569247771422844">4.3/5 stars<br/><br/><b> And then, after five minutes of silence, almost inaudibly, the old man sighed and said, more to himself than to Artyom: ‘Lord, what a splendid world we ruined..." </b><br/><br/>TW: Violence, radiation, paranoid symptoms<br/><br/>Whenever I think about this book, I think about a journey, about a lifetime of darkness and fear, about people buried under the earth, about struggling to breathe. Because that is what this book felt for me. I started it when I was sure I would fall into a reading slump, and yet, re</span>
  <span id="freeText13659569247771422844" style="display:none">4.3/5 stars<br /><br /><b> And then, after five minutes of silence, almost inaudibly, the old man sighed and said, more to himself than to Artyom: ‘Lord, what a splendid world we ruined..." </b><br /><br />TW: Violence, radiation, paranoid symptoms<br /><br />Whenever I think about this book, I think about a journey, about a lifetime of darkness and fear, about people buried under the earth, about struggling to breathe. Because that is what this book felt for me. I started it when I was sure I would fall into a reading slump, and yet, reading a bit of it every day not only helped me through it but also made me excited to read again. I was devouring this book like air, braving through travelling in pitch black caves and running from things unseen. The writing was riddled with philosophical questions and remarks, and some of them I still think about ever since I read it.<br /><br />This is a story where all characters are men, I am not gonna lie. It is one of these chunky dystopian novels that include too much, are extremely plot driven and mess with your head. And at the time, I found myself enjoying it very, very much. I thought about Artyom, found myself caring about him, ached with him and worried with him, wondered with him and ultimately connected with him. The world building was insane, the basis on Russia's history was incredible, every single detail mattered and every single mistake had a price.<br /><br />I found the discussion on cults, beliefs, desperately needing to explain things, obsessively searching for a clue to the universe's mechanisms very strong and important. The discussion on fate, duty and the need to occupy a space and do something about the world you live in were also very well-written and matched the overall theme of the story. I believe this worked exceptionally good in novel form, and am really excited to play the game too.<br /><br />Overall, I feel like this was really well written, and although it isn't the typical things I usually enjoy, it was still wonderful! (Bonus points for the absense of romance). If you are in the mood for big fiction books that will make you think a lot about where our world is heading and will give you a surreal experience, I recommend you check it out ♥ Until the next review, please remember you are all loved ♥<br />~Mary ♥</span>
  <a data-text-id="13659569247771422844" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1024069054" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1024069054" />
    <a title="David" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3335664-david"><img alt="David" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551667298p2/3335664.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1024069054?book_show_action=true">Aug 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David" href="/user/show/3335664-david">David</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/22907115-metro-2033">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Mutants in the metro, Dark Ones, Commies and Nazis in the post-apocalypse</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=russian-literature">russian-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=post-apocalyptic">post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=russia">russia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1024069054" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17401140012844405536">A nuclear war in 2013 wiped out most of the population of the world, and the remnants living underground in the Moscow subway tunnels believe they are the only humans left alive. Each station in the old metro is now its own little city-state. The main character, a young man named Artyom, is sent on a quest to another station. Along the way, he meets Nazis, Communists, Satanists, monks, cannibals, cultists, flying monsters, and mutants. The ending is ironic and grim, as befits a Russian novel tak</span>
  <span id="freeText17401140012844405536" style="display:none">A nuclear war in 2013 wiped out most of the population of the world, and the remnants living underground in the Moscow subway tunnels believe they are the only humans left alive. Each station in the old metro is now its own little city-state. The main character, a young man named Artyom, is sent on a quest to another station. Along the way, he meets Nazis, Communists, Satanists, monks, cannibals, cultists, flying monsters, and mutants. The ending is ironic and grim, as befits a Russian novel taking place after the bombs fall.<br /><br />Apparently a big cult phenomenon in Russia, which has spawned sequels and video games, <i>Metro 2033</i> reads a lot like an old-school post-holocaust fantasy, with a man of the new world journeying through the wreckage of the old one, missing the references that are left for the reader to recognize. It also reads a lot like an old-school dungeon crawl, which makes it both repetitive and fun, though I'm afraid the repetitiveness caused me to tune out at several points in the story as I listened to the audiobook.<br /><br />Artyom's quest basically consists of going from one station to the next, finding each ruled by some twisted microcosm of the old world (the Red Line, the Fourth Reich, the Watchtower, etc.), escaping, and moving on, acquiring and losing companions along the way.<br /><br />It's not hard to see how this would adapt well to a game. The writing was often psychologically deeper than your typical mutant-haunted post-apocalyptic tale, but the descriptiveness of the prose seemed to fall a little flat in translation. It's definitely a little different in tone from a Western sci-fi novel, even though it conforms to the genre fine. Had it been a little bit less of a dungeon crawl, I would probably have enjoyed it more, but after the third or fourth narrow escape from underground morlocks, I began to simply become impatient for the climax. I suspect, however, that there are a lot of references and in-jokes that didn't translate well into English.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17401140012844405536" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_113200072" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/113200072" />
    <a title="Eric Piotrowski" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/233776-eric-piotrowski"><img alt="Eric Piotrowski" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442894700p2/233776.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/113200072?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eric Piotrowski" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eric Piotrowski" href="/user/show/233776-eric-piotrowski">Eric Piotrowski</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9783453532984" href="/book/show/5558786-metro-2033">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/233776-eric-piotrowski?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/233776-eric-piotrowski?shelf=philosophy">philosophy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/233776-eric-piotrowski?shelf=novels">novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer113200072" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3473675264170386774">I began reading this book several months ago, since I'm eager to play the video game that was recently adapted from it. I expected to get a standard post-apocalyptic adventure novel, and this is what I got -- for 80% of the book. The other 20% is filled with bleak philosophizing and clouds of uncertainty that creep around the main character, like the weird sounds and unsettling environs of the dessicated metro itself.<br/><br/>Then, in the last ten pages, this wave of conceptualization leaps out of the sh</span>
  <span id="freeText3473675264170386774" style="display:none">I began reading this book several months ago, since I'm eager to play the video game that was recently adapted from it. I expected to get a standard post-apocalyptic adventure novel, and this is what I got -- for 80% of the book. The other 20% is filled with bleak philosophizing and clouds of uncertainty that creep around the main character, like the weird sounds and unsettling environs of the dessicated metro itself.<br /><br />Then, in the last ten pages, this wave of conceptualization leaps out of the shadows and pounces on the reader, nearly suffocating her/him. The profound impact of the philosophy and concept are staggering; they left me with a reeling sense of impact, not unlike the first time I watched <i>The Usual Suspects</i> or finished reading <i>Solaris</i>.<br /><br />Glukhovsky's style is sharp and he mixes silly disconnected events with politics, allegory, and a thin film of background theorizing which seem to go nowhere. Sorting through the mental rubble as the characters trek through physical rubble. A very intoxicating mix of story and ideas.<br /><br />Highly recommended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3473675264170386774" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review113200072">

<div id="review_1857267891" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1857267891" />
    <a title="Igor Ljubuncic" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10471943-igor-ljubuncic"><img alt="Igor Ljubuncic" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492196263p2/10471943.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1857267891?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Igor Ljubuncic" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Igor Ljubuncic" href="/user/show/10471943-igor-ljubuncic">Igor Ljubuncic</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10471943-igor-ljubuncic?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10471943-igor-ljubuncic?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10471943-igor-ljubuncic?shelf=russian">russian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10471943-igor-ljubuncic?shelf=zombies">zombies</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1857267891" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8514752299029026608">Well, this was an odd experience.<br/><br/>I actually stopped reading about 100 pages in, and I'm not going to rate this.<br/><br/>On one hand, the theme is original, there's a real sense of dread and despair, and the futuristic Moscow metro system that houses the few survivors of the apocalypse that has gripped the world feels like a bleak, harsh place.<br/><br/>On the other, the writing progresses slowly. Too slowly. It reminds me somewhat of the late 19th century novels, where the plot kind of builds up and builds up and </span>
  <span id="freeText8514752299029026608" style="display:none">Well, this was an odd experience.<br /><br />I actually stopped reading about 100 pages in, and I'm not going to rate this.<br /><br />On one hand, the theme is original, there's a real sense of dread and despair, and the futuristic Moscow metro system that houses the few survivors of the apocalypse that has gripped the world feels like a bleak, harsh place.<br /><br />On the other, the writing progresses slowly. Too slowly. It reminds me somewhat of the late 19th century novels, where the plot kind of builds up and builds up and keeps building up, but nothing happens. You're waiting for that something to kick the action off, but it's just not coming. And that feels exhausting after a while. There are way too many descriptions and pondering, and quite a few discrepancies in what the protagonist(s) do. I know there's a dark secret in the metro system, and I want to learn it, but I can't be bothered going through so many filler pages without anything substantial taking place, plot-wise.<br /><br />Well, maybe I'll pick this up again one day, but for now, it didn't work for me.<br /><br />Igor</span>
  <a data-text-id="8514752299029026608" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16555616072642587568">I DNFed this book at 34%. This book was recommended to me by my boyfriend who played the video game based off of this book, and also listened to this book on audio.<br/><br/>I really wanted to like this book. I really did, but I couldn’t get past the author’s tendency to go on and on about things I didn’t think really mattered or had anything to do with the progression of the book. This book is a monster in size, which was intimidating as well. I did appreciate the world and the concept, as well as the fa</span>
  <span id="freeText16555616072642587568" style="display:none">I DNFed this book at 34%. This book was recommended to me by my boyfriend who played the video game based off of this book, and also listened to this book on audio.<br /><br />I really wanted to like this book. I really did, but I couldn’t get past the author’s tendency to go on and on about things I didn’t think really mattered or had anything to do with the progression of the book. This book is a monster in size, which was intimidating as well. I did appreciate the world and the concept, as well as the fact this is set in Moscow in a metro station. I just don’t feel this was executed well. It could be from translation, but I’ve never really liked books that seem to speak on and on about things that don’t really matter.</span>

<div id="review_618344730" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/618344730" />
    <a title="Dominique Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20464196-dominique-rose"><img alt="Dominique Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368936721p2/20464196.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/618344730?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dominique Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dominique Rose" href="/user/show/20464196-dominique-rose">Dominique Rose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9783453532984" href="/book/show/5558786-metro-2033">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20464196-dominique-rose?shelf=sci-fi-and-fantasy">sci-fi-and-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer618344730&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer618344730" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2791730485340537361">I was so excited to get into this book! I love exploring a unique apocalyptic world and this one sounded like a winner. Not knowing much about the Moscow Metro, I spent a happy half hour scrolling through google images of its glamourous stations. That, unfortunately, was the most enjoyment I got out of the whole experience.<br/><br/>My copy of Metro 2033 was an English translation of the Russian novel, and I really do wish I could have read the original. There were so many moments where either there wasn’</span>
  <span id="freeText2791730485340537361" style="display:none">I was so excited to get into this book! I love exploring a unique apocalyptic world and this one sounded like a winner. Not knowing much about the Moscow Metro, I spent a happy half hour scrolling through google images of its glamourous stations. That, unfortunately, was the most enjoyment I got out of the whole experience.<br /><br />My copy of Metro 2033 was an English translation of the Russian novel, and I really do wish I could have read the original. There were so many moments where either there wasn’t an equivalent phrase in English, or the translator was not capable enough to find one. Take the following extract:<br /><br />“It was a torn tab – a circle of thick rubberised substance, about seven centimetres in diameter. <br /><br />On one side it was completely black, on the other was portrayed the intersection of three incomprehensible oblong objects on a dark background, not unlike one of the six-pointed paper snowflakes with which they decorated VDNKh for the New Year.<br /><br />One of the objects was standing upright and Artyom recognised it as a cartridge from a machine gun or a sniper’s rifle, but with wings attached to the bottom. But he did not recognise the other two identical, yellow ones, with rings on both sides. The mysterious snowflake was enclosed in a stylised wreath, such as on old cockades, and there were letters around the circle of the tab.”<br /><br />Um? I must have reread that 4 or 5 times to try make some sense of it. I was unsuccessful.<br /><br />It almost felt as though there should have been a third person in the writing process. The author, obviously; the translator; and a second, English-speaking author to help give some fluidity and life back to the prose. Or maybe just the author plus a better translator.<br /><br />The names of the stations also remain in their original format, and it was definitely a challenge finding them on the accompanying map, but I kind of enjoyed that.<br /><br />So, taking the technical issues into account, I really wanted to give the benefit of the doubt and say maybe I would have enjoyed this book more if I had read it straight from Glukhovsky’s hand. But some of the issues looked to be more than just a case of lost in translation.<br /><br />I found the protagonist, Artyom, to be flat. We get to hear a lot about his emerging philosophies and determination to complete his quest, but we never learn much about the man himself. He drifts passively through the plot, barely interacting with the many secondary characters other than to follow them to his next destination. He sees and experiences so many new things, yet he remains untouched and unchanged by them. In a story that relies heavily upon the traditional quest format, each new obstacle became tedious and repetitive in its inability to effect the hero and I became disengaged well before he reached his goal.<br /><br />And when he did reach that destination? Well, let’s just say I felt the book really should have ended there. The cannibals, Metro 2, the Kremlin creature, these all should have either been integrated into the book earlier or left for the sequel. The endless and repetitive reflections on fate could have been left out altogether, since they still made no impact on Artyom himself. For me, the visits to the surface were the most interesting parts of the book and, if they were tied in with the final few pages, would have made for a much more satisfying conclusion.<br /><br />Oh, and where were the women? There wasn’t a single female character that wasn’t a mother or child weeping in the background. Not one. Come on, Dmitry.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2791730485340537361" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_982079235" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/982079235" />
    <a title="Casey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7010826-casey"><img alt="Casey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1526233744p2/7010826.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/982079235?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Casey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Casey" href="/user/show/7010826-casey">Casey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781491508183" href="/book/show/20671315-metro-2033">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7010826-casey?shelf=suspense-thrillers">suspense-thrillers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer982079235" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12669838532894834109">While listening to this audiobook, I jotted down a few phrases that sprang to the forefront of my consciousness.<br/><br/>* Good writing<br/>* Elegant exposition<br/>* Predominantly solid pacing – turns suspect at the end<br/>* Nice management of tension – slackens at climax<br/>* Strong atmosphere - establishes dark and closed-in spaces<br/>* <u>Fantastic</u> narrator - Rupert Degas nails the reading<br/><br/>Without question, I recommend this book. I strongly suggest you listen to the audiobook. You might feel a little bummed at the end, but th</span>
  <span id="freeText12669838532894834109" style="display:none">While listening to this audiobook, I jotted down a few phrases that sprang to the forefront of my consciousness.<br /><br />* Good writing<br />* Elegant exposition<br />* Predominantly solid pacing – turns suspect at the end<br />* Nice management of tension – slackens at climax<br />* Strong atmosphere - establishes dark and closed-in spaces<br />* <u>Fantastic</u> narrator - Rupert Degas nails the reading<br /><br />Without question, I recommend this book. I strongly suggest you listen to the audiobook. You might feel a little bummed at the end, but the writing is strong enough to support its fumbled conclusion.<br /><br />Dmitry Glukhovsky's <i>Metro 2033</i>, book 1 in the Metro Series, offers an interesting take on the travel/road narrative. Draw your own academic conclusions, but for the most part, humans yet blindly stumble in the dark, face self-inflicted nuclear/biological disaster, and unseen things are hungry. But worry not; man yet possesses fire, fear, weapons, and hatred. What we do not possess appears to be an accurate map, foresight, or the ability to think outside our own skull.<br /><br />I reveled in the atmosphere. A bunch of people crammed into underground tunnels, forced to keep watch by firelight, eating mushrooms, pork, and rodents, became nearly a corporeal experience. Different metro stations setting up their own community, the need for passports for those wishing to travel between stations, and the various creation/destruction myths surrounding each group, delivers a strong sense of fractured and desperate realism.<br /><br />The story is okay, but for me, the writing is what shined brightest. The only character I felt remotely invested with was a man named Hunter. The other players in this tale, while multifaceted to a degree, lacked a depth and drive that I feel is paramount for investable and memorable characters.<br /><br />As noted above, Rupert Degas is amazing. His rhythm and talents for infusing mood into speech takes flight in this reading. I can't speak for the accent accuracy, but I can tell you that Degas's delivery drew me in and made me feel the darkness.<br /><br />I loved the library excursion. So good! Really wished there'd been more story in this setting. The scene with the librarian playing with the flashlight was surprisingly moving.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12669838532894834109" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('d900y2+hDx1WBvoaqZrHGKQVDSGy9ftR+leG9MGnu51N+10Z1P/GdfEtTnteb83Hckrq6Xx4dTahKcBFDORJBw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ldx+R7q6UXfDvysi5kYOw0Z/lrNsq4OcMofkaWUkQwGv+heVAeSYH2SUn0MRswQckCBxe6ImDftp+aLYqGexmw==')})
  }

Nie mamy już gdzie wrócić. Ale nikt nie jest w stanie pozbawić nas najważniejszego: hartu ducha. Dzisiaj, jak nigdy, powinniśmy pozostać silni, dlatego że przed nami ostatnie, być może najistotniejsze wyzwanie. Cokolwiek się stanie, trzeba odszukać sprawców wybuchu i rozliczyć się z nimi za śmierć naszych bliskich.\n\nNa oczach załogi Babla, pływającej platformy wiertniczej, mieszkańcy Moszcznego giną w ogniu eksplozji nuklearnej. Kto i dlaczego podniósł rękę na pokojową społeczność wyspy, niwecząc nadzieje na lepszą przyszłość dla garstki ocalałych z Katastrofy? Podejrzenie pada na mieszkańców petersburskiego metra, którzy otrzymują ultimatum: w ciągu tygodnia muszą ustalić winnych. Inaczej wszyscy podzielą los unicestwionej wyspy… Śledztwo spoczywa na barkach stalkera Tarana. Sytuację komplikuje niespodziewane zniknięcie Gleba, jego przybranego syna. Mnożą się pytania, a droga do prawdy jest trudna. Odpowiedzi są bowiem ukryte w mroku – na samym dnie ludzkiej duszy.\n\nSkażony świat, dzikie bestie, głód – to tylko opakowanie, tło, zewnętrzna strona mroku. Z tym nauczyliśmy się już walczyć. Prawdziwy mrok jest wewnątrz, w naszych głowach. The scientists go missing and a search and rescue operation is launched. For Mikhailo Tarasov, officer in the armed forces who desperately try to contain the Exclusion Zone, this mutant-infested wilderness is his home turf. Tarasov is aided by unlikely allies - outcasts, adventurers, renegade US Marines and a mysterious woman who appears to be the keeper of dark secrets. But beyond all the perils, the ultimate danger awaits: betrayal. The noir, post-apocalyptic narrative of S.T.A.L.K.E.R.: Southern Comfort goes is a contemporary voyage into the heart of darkness, where not only the laws of physics are bent but the rules of the outside world as well. This is an alternative reality where outcasts prevail, the oppressed take revenge and the faithful revolt.  &quot;&quot;Whatever power had created the Zone, it has outsmarted us and it has happened again. You will look at the New Zone with fresh eyes... like Strelok did here when everything began.&quot;&quot; Major Alexander Degtyarev, 2014<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"3420009170275045134\" href=\"#\" <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15269642740209449542">Dmitry Glukhovsky (Russian: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6434478._' rel='nofollow noopener'>Дмитрий Глуховский</a>) is a professional Russian author and journalist. Glukhovsky started in 2002 by publishing his first novel, Metro 2033, on his own website to be viewed for free. The novel has later become an interactive experiment, drawing in many readers, and has since been made into a video game for the Xbox 360 console and PC. Glukhovsky is known in Russia for his</span>
  <span id="freeText15269642740209449542" style="display:none">Dmitry Glukhovsky (Russian: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6434478._" rel="nofollow noopener">Дмитрий Глуховский</a>) is a professional Russian author and journalist. Glukhovsky started in 2002 by publishing his first novel, Metro 2033, on his own website to be viewed for free. The novel has later become an interactive experiment, drawing in many readers, and has since been made into a video game for the Xbox 360 console and PC. Glukhovsky is known in Russia for his novels Metro 2033 and "It's Getting Darker". He is also an author of a series of satirical "Stories of Motherland" criticizing today's Russia.<br />As a journalist, Dmitry Glukhovsky has worked for EuroNews TV in France, Deutsche Welle, and RT. In 2008-2009 he worked as a radio host of a Mayak Radio Station. He writes columns for Harper’s Bazaar, l’Officiel and Playboy.<br />He has lived in Israel, Germany and France and speaks English, French, German, Hebrew and Spanish as well as his native Russian.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15269642740209449542" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
